Sports

Putting the Sixteen-Pound Shot Put 108

Is an Old Track and Field Event in China 109

Old Record: 11.20 Meters 110

Held by Meng Jimao 111

Because the Far Eastern Athletics Games will use the sixteen-pound shot put in the next session, this year's National Games have also decided to follow the Far Eastern rules, abandon the twelve-pound shot put, and restore the old sixteen-pound shot put event in China. Recently, many newspapers have said that the sixteen-pound shot put is a new event and that China has no old records to refer to. In fact, this is not accurate. According to the regulations used at the beginning of track and field in China at the end of the Qing Dynasty, the sixteen-pound shot put was adopted in accordance with world regulations. In 1919, the twelve-pound shot put was adopted. It has been twelve years since then that we have restored the ancient event of our country. The first Far Eastern Games also used the sixteen-pound shot put. From the fifth session onwards, because China, Japan, and the Philippines felt that their physical strength was insufficient, the twelve-pound shot put was adopted. The adoption of the sixteen-pound shot put again in the next session is also a restoration of the original state and is by no means a newly added event. The highest records of the two shot put events in the Far East are listed below. Sixteen-pound shot put: Alavaris (Philippines), 11.34 meters, 4th session. Twelve-pound shot put: Shizuo Takada (Japan), 15.80 meters, 9th session. The highest record for the sixteen-pound shot put in China was 10.90 meters, held by Gao Siyang in 1913, created in Hongkou Park, Shanghai. The national record after that was 11.20 meters, set by Meng Jimao in 1919 at the Far Eastern Games in Manila, Philippines, on May 12 of that year. Meng participated in the third and fourth sessions of the Games and was selected for the shot put competition. From this, it can be proved that the sixteen-pound shot put is not a newly added event in China but is definitely an old one. The record of Mr. Meng should also be used as the standard for the new and old records in this year's National Games.

Local News

How Strange, the Chinese 125

Request to Extend the Concession 126

Large Headline in the "Dà Měi Evening News"

Chinese Request to the Municipal Council

A Request that Advisor Feitham Dared Not Make

Shanghai Western Merchants and Residents are Heartbroken and Frantic

Since the late Qing Dynasty, due to ignorance of foreign affairs, the government did not want Chinese and foreigners to live together, so it demarcated land in treaty ports for foreign merchants to reside in. Moreover, due to the incompetence of officials, they relinquished their administrative rights over the land, creating the concessions of today. As a result, foreigners issue orders and govern, reversing the roles of guest and host, causing the Chinese, within their own country, to be governed by foreigners, becoming a rare phenomenon in ancient and modern times. This has been the case for more than eighty years. Fortunately, in recent times, people's intelligence has been awakened day by day, and the movement to restore national rights is united from top to bottom, competing to recover lost rights. The British concessions in Hankou, Xiamen, and the Belgian concession in Tianjin have been returned one after another. Now we are engaged in the complete recovery. Yet, at this time, there is a request to extend the concessions, and it comes from merchants and residents in western Shanghai. Is this not a shocking and strange thing to hear? If this move came from foreigners or was fabricated by two or three stubborn foreigners, it could still be seen as their last struggle, merely earning them ridicule for not knowing the times. We would not find it strange. However, according to the headline in the "Dà Měi Evening News," it is proclaimed in large letters that "Chinese Request to the Municipal Council." If this news is indeed true, then these Chinese can truly be said to be heartbroken and frantic, willing to be foreign slaves. The people of our entire country must investigate this matter clearly and immediately correct it, lest it be passed down and spread abroad, making the world laugh, causing all 400 million of our compatriots to be ashamed, and giving Westerners an excuse to refuse to return the concessions.

According to the "Dà Měi Evening News," merchants and residents from Zhujiaqiao, Wangjialou (transliteration), and Shengjiaqiao (transliteration) in western Shanghai have jointly requested the Municipal Council to extend the concession to include the three places and the areas of roads built beyond the borders. They want to purchase land in Zhujiaqiao, Caojiadu, and Shengjiaqiao along Hongqiao Road to set up patrol police posts, lay tram tracks on Hongqiao and Bailinan Roads, pave the roads in western Shanghai into asphalt roads, add streetlights, and collect patrol police taxes from shops, residents, and factories on each road to fund the construction. The reasons they give for requesting the extension of the concession are that there are many factories in western Shanghai, and the number of shops and residences of Chinese and foreigners is increasing daily. The market is gradually becoming prosperous, but residents are greatly inconvenienced due to the lack of running water and streetlights, and especially because there are no police patrols, which often leads to robberies. According to this, such problems can be easily solved once the problem of roads built beyond the borders is resolved. If the Shanghai concessions can be recovered, it would be even less of a problem. Even Judge Feitham, hired by the Municipal Council to preserve the concessions, did not dare to openly advocate the extension of the concessions, but only proposed to form a Sino-foreign joint municipal authority in the areas of roads built beyond the borders. What do these merchants and residents see or what do they benefit from wanting to extend the concessions?

Association for Raising Funds for Emergency Flood Relief in Various Provinces

Inaugural Meeting Tomorrow 127

Address: City Chamber of Commerce

Time: 5:00 PM

Recognizing that the recent floods have spread everywhere, causing severe disasters, leaving tens of millions of people homeless, prominent figures from the political and business circles of this city, such as Yu Qiaqing, Zhang Zhijiang, Wang Xiaolai, and Xu Shiying, have specially initiated the Shanghai Preparatory Office for Raising Funds for Emergency Flood Relief in Various Provinces, and have scheduled the second preparatory meeting for today at 5:00 PM, and the inaugural meeting for tomorrow at 5:00 PM, to be held at the City Chamber of Commerce. The letter issued by the preparatory office yesterday is recorded below:

Notice of Today's Preparatory Meeting: Respectfully inform you that due to the inaugural meeting of this preparatory office to be held at the City Chamber of Commerce on the afternoon of the 6th, all matters must be actively carried out. It is scheduled to hold another preparatory meeting at 5:00 PM on the afternoon of the 5th. We hereby send this letter and respectfully request your presence on time to discuss matters together. Sincerely wishing you well.

Notice of the Inaugural Meeting: Respectfully inform you that since the beginning of summer this year, there has been continuous rain, mountain torrents have erupted, and ditches and streams have overflowed. The provinces of Sichuan, Guangdong, Hunan, Hubei, Henan, Shandong, Anhui, Jiangxi, Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Fujian, Hebei, Jilin, Heilongjiang, and Rehe have all become flooded areas. The extent of the disaster is unprecedented in a century. Fields and houses are submerged, and people and livestock are swept away. The livelihood of farmers for a year is thus hopeless. All industrial and commercial sectors are also indirectly affected. If we do not urgently rescue them, then tens of millions of old, weak, and helpless disaster victims without clothes, food, or shelter will fall into ditches and gullies, and the strong will flee in all directions. The rebellious ones may even take risks. Looking to the future, we cannot help but shudder. Therefore, we believe that the current floods in various provinces are of great social importance, and relief is urgently needed. We have specially united with various organizations and philanthropists to organize the Shanghai Association for Raising Funds for Emergency Flood Relief in Various Provinces to save our groaning and suffering compatriots and fulfill our duty to help. We have now been organized and have scheduled the inaugural meeting for 6:00 PM on the afternoon of the 6th of this month at the City Chamber of Commerce. We have also prepared a simple vegetarian meal to listen to your teachings. We have always admired your benevolence and concern for the hungry and drowning, and your willingness to raise your arms to rescue them. We believe you share our sympathy. We earnestly request your early arrival to provide full guidance and jointly plan the progress. With a hundred bows, we await your arrival and sincerely wish you well. Respectfully informed by the Preparatory Office of the Shanghai Association for Raising Funds for Emergency Flood Relief in Various Provinces, Yu Qiaqing, Qin Runqing, Du Yuesheng, Li Jin, Zhang Zhijiang, Lin Kanghou, Chen Guangfu, Wu Yunzhai, Xu Shiying, Zhu Qinglan, Wen Lanting, Wu Zhihao, Zhang Qun, Niu Yongjian, Huang Qinglan, Shi Liangcai, Wang Zhen, Zhang Gongquan, Wang Yansong, Wang Boqi, Wang Xiaolai, Xie Hengchuang, Zhang Xiaolin, Liu Zhanen, and colleagues.

Xu Shiying's Telegram: The Shanghai Preparatory Office for Raising Funds for Emergency Flood Relief in Various Provinces received a telegram from Committee Member Xu Shiying from Nanjing yesterday, stating that he is scheduled to come to Shanghai today (the 5th) to attend the meeting on the 6th.

More Notes on the Flood's Obstruction of Navigation 128

Inland Rivers, the Yangtze River, Coastal Areas

The floods in various places have hindered navigation, as has been reported repeatedly in this newspaper. Although the weather has been clear recently, navigation, whether on inland rivers, the Yangtze River, or coastal areas, is still affected by the floods. The recent situation is reported again as follows:

Anhui Goods Cannot Be Transported: The import and export of goods to and from Wuhu in southern Anhui and Anqing in northern Anhui along the Yangtze River have been almost completely blocked by the various shipping companies in this city due to the impact of the recent floods. The reason is that the wharf boats in both ports are already full of passengers and goods, and inland transportation is isolated by the water, making it impossible to load and unload. Therefore, in recent days, the various Yangtze River steamers in Shanghai have stopped loading goods to Wuhu, Anqing, etc., and the arrival of goods from the two places has also been cut off.

Shenjiao Steamer Blocked from Returning: Inland river steamers have been blocked and stopped by the flood for almost a month. The China Merchants Bureau's Shenjiao regular steamer started a trial run on the 3rd in preparation for resuming service. Unexpectedly, when the ship reached the Baihedang area, it was stopped by the water surveyors sent by Qingpu County and was not allowed to proceed. The ship returned to Shanghai as before. Qingpu County has now issued a notice stating that small steamers to Qingpu and Zhujiajiao will only be allowed to operate on a trial basis starting on the 6th. Therefore, the goods and passengers on the ship were all transferred to be transported tomorrow.

After the Hengtong Sank: The accident of the Hengtong small steamer sinking in Bihuba, Shaobo, has been reported previously. It is now learned that the ship was carrying a battalion of infantry from Liang Guanying's 25th Army to Qingjiangpu. The people on board initially thought that it was very dangerous to operate the ship at night, but they were violently beaten by those forcing the ship to sail. They were then forced to set sail, which resulted in a collision with a civilian boat's iron anchor, causing the ship to break and sink. The soldiers have now been transferred from Shaobo to Qingjiang, and the China Merchants Inland River Bureau has reported the truth of the accident to the Zhejiang Construction Department, requesting that they prevent the forced sailing of ships during the flood period.

Difficult to Unload Goods in Hankou: The flood in Hankou has not completely receded. Yesterday, various shipping companies in this city received another telegram from Hankou, stating that the water in Hankou is even greater, with some low-lying warehouses being flooded to a depth of six feet, and even higher warehouses being flooded to a depth of one foot. All goods arriving in Hankou are being unloaded onto barges and cannot be directly loaded onto the warehouses. Those who had taken early precautions mostly used sandbags and mud to build enclosures to block the water. In recent days, the goods going to Hankou from this city have been greatly reduced.

Difficult to Navigate Baihe River: The Baihe River in Tianjin is silted up, with a draft of only eight feet. Shanghai-bound commercial ships such as Fusheng and Xinfeng have successively run aground due to silting at Tanggu Port. Although the water has risen recently, the silt has also increased, making navigation even more difficult. When the Shunlun arrives at Tanggu, it also runs aground. It has now been towed out. At present, ships arriving in Tianjin are all in Dagu, first transferring the goods before proceeding to the port.

Continued Receipt of Letters and Telegrams Requesting Disaster Relief 129

The Shanghai Chinese and Foreign Charity Relief Association has continued to receive letters and telegrams from various counties in Anhui requesting flood relief, as follows: (1) A letter from Fanchang County states, "Fanchang County is unfortunate. Since the beginning of summer, there has been continuous rain, and mountain torrents have caused dozens of large and small dikes to collapse one after another. The fields have become flooded areas, and the streets are like lakeshores. In recent days, there have been violent storms and heavy rains. Waves of three to five zhang high rise suddenly, like overturning the sea and moving mountains. For hundreds of li, sand and stones fly, directly pressing the sky and rolling the earth. Starving people are everywhere, and their faces are emaciated. Relief is urgently needed. Please help." (2) A telegram from fellow villagers from Wuwei Province states, "The Huangsitan embankment in Wuwei County has collapsed, and hundreds of embankments in the county have collapsed at the same time. People, livestock, and fields have been tragically swept away. The disaster is overwhelming, and the sound of crying shakes the earth. Please urgently provide relief to save 800,000 dying disaster victims." (3) A letter from the Dangtu County Red Cross Branch states, "Dangtu is located on the Yangtze River and is low-lying. Since the beginning of summer, there has been heavy rain, continuously for days. Mountain torrents have poured down, and the rivers and lakes have risen sharply. The water is several feet deep on flat ground. In addition, the strong wind has broken all the embankments, turning them into a vast expanse of water. People, livestock, houses, and farm implements have been swept away. The sound of weeping is unbearable to hear, and mourning geese are everywhere. Relief is urgently needed. Please find a way to provide urgent relief to save the situation." (4) A letter from the Woyang County Government states, "This year, there was continuous rain in early July, and there were heavy rains on the 18th and 23rd and 24th, coupled with storms. The entire county was flooded, and seedlings and houses were swept away. The sound of crying is tragic. At the moment, there is no food or grass, and people are crying for food. Please provide relief." (5) A letter from the Dingyuan County Chamber of Commerce states, "Since the beginning of July, the county has been hit by continuous rain, day and night. Within the city, the streets have become canals. In the rural areas, mountain torrents have erupted, turning everything into a flooded area. Settlements have been razed to the ground, and people and livestock have drowned one after another. Houses and tombs have been washed away. The exact number of deaths cannot be determined. It is estimated that there are currently more than 20,000 to 30,000 households homeless and waiting to die. Please allocate large sums of money to provide urgent relief to save the survivors." Also, a letter from the Kunshan County Farmers' Association in Jiangsu Province states, "Kunshan County has been hit by torrential rains for the past half month, day and night. Livestock have been swept away, seedlings have been submerged, and embankments have completely collapsed. The fields have become flooded areas, houses are leaning, and people lack food. The severity of the disaster is unprecedented in decades. Please raise emergency relief to relieve the suffering."

Announcement by the Municipal Government

Rules for Penalties for Collection of Business Tax 132

The Municipal Finance Bureau previously drafted the draft rules for penalties for collection of business tax in this city, totaling twelve articles, in accordance with Article 18 of the regulations for collection of business tax in this city, and submitted them to the municipal government for review and instructions. It is heard that the municipal government has made some revisions and announced them on Monday. The articles are as follows:

Article 1. These rules are formulated in accordance with the provisions of Article 18 of the regulations for the collection of business tax in this city. Article 2. Violations of Article 11, Article 17 of the regulations for the collection of business tax in this city, and Article 3 of the implementation rules, such as failing to apply for a business license or failing to renew it when required, will be punished as follows, in addition to being ordered to apply for renewal separately: (A) For the first offense, a fine of one to ten yuan will be imposed. (B) For the second offense, a fine of ten to twenty yuan will be imposed. (C) For violations of more than two times, a fine of twenty to thirty yuan will be imposed. Article 3. Violations of Article 11 and Article 12 of the regulations for the collection of business tax in this city, such as underreporting the amount of business capital or turnover, will be punished as follows, in addition to being ordered to pay the supplementary tax: (A) For the first offense, a fine of one to two times the amount of the unpaid tax will be imposed. (B) For the second offense, a fine of two to five times the amount of the unpaid tax will be imposed. (C) For violations of more than two times, a fine of five to ten times the amount of the unpaid tax will be imposed. Article 4. Violations of Article 11 and Article 12 of the regulations for the collection of business tax in this city, such as concealing and failing to report, will be punished as follows, in addition to being ordered to pay the supplementary tax: (A) For the first offense, a fine of three to five times the amount of the unpaid tax will be imposed. (B) For the second offense, a fine of five to ten times the amount of the unpaid tax will be imposed. (C) For violations of more than two times, a fine of ten to fifteen times the amount of the unpaid tax will be imposed. Article 5. Violations of Article 4 of the implementation rules of the regulations for the collection of business tax in this city, such as falsifying accounting books and making false records, will be punished as follows, in addition to being ordered to pay the supplementary tax: (A) For the first offense, a fine of five to ten times the amount of the unpaid tax will be imposed. (B) For the second offense, a fine of ten to fifteen times the amount of the unpaid tax will be imposed. (C) For violations of more than two times, a fine of fifteen to twenty times the amount of the unpaid tax will be imposed. Article 6. If a business operator fails to pay the tax due for each quarter after a delay of more than one month, a late payment penalty of one-tenth will be added. If the delay is more than two months, a late payment penalty of two-tenths will be added. If the delay is more than three months, the business tax investigation certificate may be revoked, and the unpaid tax and late payment penalty will still be pursued. However, if the delay is due to the delay of the collecting agency in charge, no late payment penalty will be added, and the above-mentioned investigation certificate will be exempt from revocation. Article 7. Those whose business investigation certificate has been revoked due to late payment of business tax may not reapply for the above-mentioned investigation certificate unless the tax and penalty have been paid in full. Article 8. The fines imposed in accordance with these rules shall be notified by the collecting agency in charge to the penalized party for compliance and payment, and a fine receipt shall be filled out and given when the fine is paid. The aforementioned fine notification and fine receipt shall be prepared by the Finance Bureau and filled out by the collecting agency in charge. Article 9. If the penalized party refuses to comply with the imposed fine, the collecting agency in charge may hand it over to the local public security bureau or district office for enforcement, or submit it to the Finance Bureau for review and handling. Article 10. Regardless of whether the fine imposed in accordance with these rules is discovered and punished by the personnel of the collecting agency in charge, or by an outsider's report, 40% of the fine may be extracted as a reward, and the remaining 60% shall be reported and remitted along with the collected taxes. The method for awarding the reward will be determined separately. Article 11. If there are any matters not covered in these rules, the Finance Bureau may revise them at any time and submit them to the municipal government for approval and record. Article 12. These rules shall be implemented from the date of promulgation after being approved by the municipal government.

Business Tax Collected Separately for Main and Branch Stores 133

The City Chamber of Commerce sent a letter to the Rubber, Hardware, and Car Parts Industry Association yesterday, stating, "Regarding your association's letter stating that some members have branch stores in Jiangsu, and asking whether the business tax can be paid together by the main store in Shanghai, and requesting verification and reply, we have telegraphed the Ministry of Finance for an explanation. We now forward the reply from the Ministry of Finance, numbered Fu Zi 6737: 'We have received your telegram. Shanghai is a city directly under the Executive Yuan and is not within the administrative area of Jiangsu Province. Separate regulations have been formulated for the collection of business tax, and they have been submitted to the Ministry for revision and forwarding for compliance. For various businesses that have a main store or main factory in Shanghai and branch stores or branch factories in other provinces, the business tax should be collected separately. Article 15 of the Regulations for the Collection of Business Tax in Jiangsu Province is not inconsistent. The information mentioned in your telegram is slightly misunderstood regarding the separate handling of provinces and cities.' We hereby forward a copy for your information."

Resolution of the China-Europe Shipping Dispute 135

Freight Rates Rise Again Opportunistically

In the early spring of this year, a fierce shipping dispute occurred on the Shanghai-Europe route. At that time, freight rates were reduced competitively and rebates were abused, and Japanese ships further disrupted the situation, resulting in an unregulated chaos in the European line. For several months, all shipping companies suffered. Now, the Dutch shipping company, the main instigator of the dispute, has realized that this move is a mistake, so it has stopped the fierce competition and is willing to cooperate with other shipping companies. European shipping has returned to its original state, and export freight rates have now been announced to increase. The results of the investigation are recorded in detail below. This is closely related to international trade and China's foreign export business.

Dutch Ships Rejoin the Association The Dutch East Asia Shipping Company, managed by the Java Company in Shanghai, operates on the Shanghai-Europe route to England, France, Belgium, Germany, and the Netherlands. It has more than 20 ships of six to seven thousand tons each, traveling between China and the Netherlands. Various foreign ships on the European line have formed an association, which sets the rise and fall of export freight rates, which should be observed by all. Dutch ships are also members of the association. This year, the company declared its withdrawal from the association in early spring due to poor export business, intending to be unrestricted and able to freely reduce prices in order to attract more cargo. At that time, after the company withdrew from the association, it greatly reduced freight rates. The shipping companies in the association also collectively agreed to reduce prices in order to prevent Dutch ships from taking advantage. As a result, export freight rates on the China-Europe line were reduced by one-half or two-tenths after this incident. For several months, the Dutch shipping business has not improved at all due to the joint reduction of fees. Export business is worse than before. The income after the price reduction is even less, and the losses in recent months have been considerable. Now, the company has realized that the previous proposal was a mistake, so it has asked the association to rejoin as a member, expressing cooperation. The association submitted this matter for discussion, and the shipping companies also felt that accompanying the price reduction was not a good idea, so they allowed it to join as a member. Thus, the dispute was resolved.

Increase in European Freight Rates After the association resolved the issue of the Dutch ship joining the association, it proposed to increase the export freight rates from Shanghai to Europe immediately in order to make up for the previous hidden losses. With the unanimous agreement of the representatives of the shipping companies, the association renegotiated the freight rates for various goods. Some rose by two-tenths of the original price, while others rose by six-tenths. Yesterday, the agreement was reached, and the new freight rate list was distributed to the members, ordering them to implement it immediately. The shipping companies have now notified the export customers. The new price list is specially recorded as follows (the unit in the table is ton, A price is without commission, B price is with commission):

Commodity A New Price Original Price B New Price Original Price

Shillings Shillings Shillings Shillings

Ore 32 27 35 30

Egg Yolk 68 45 75 50

Mineral Seedlings 45 41 50 45

Peanuts 61 45 68 50

Pig Bristles 100 80 110 90

Waste Hemp 54 50 60 55

Ramie 54 50 60 55

Waste Cotton 32 25 35 27

Wet Albumin 58 36 64 40

Egg Powder 68 45 75 50

Packed Wool 58 54 64 60

Five Pecks of Seeds 100 72 110 80

The above are all price increases. However, cotton cake has been reduced in price, from 32 shillings to 27 shillings, because very little of this cargo is shipped to Europe. The above commodities are major exports, so the freight rate dispute has been settled. From yesterday, shipping companies will charge according to the new prices.

Printing Industry Still Not Back in Operation Yesterday 136

Workers Resuming Work Still Implementing Eight Hours

Employers Refuse and Send Representatives to Petition Again

Social Affairs Bureau Scheduled to Summon for Questioning Today

After the Shanghai Printing Industry Association notified all colleagues to suspend business, the Social Affairs Bureau ordered them to resume work immediately and scheduled a mediation today. However, all colleagues refused because the workers were still implementing eight-hour work days. Therefore, they are still suspended. The information obtained yesterday is recorded in detail below:

Stop Suspension The Social Affairs Bureau ordered the Printing Industry Association and the Printing Industry Workers' Union: "Order to comply with the matter. Although Article 8 of the Factory Law stipulates that the working hours of workers shall be eight hours in principle, it also allows exceptions to extend to ten hours. Moreover, whether the factories in the industry are all subject to the Factory Law is still under investigation. The labor and management of the industry suddenly stopped working due to the issue of working hours, which is inappropriate. In addition to separate orders, we urgently order you to comply, quickly resume normal work and wait for this bureau to investigate and verify, and do not violate the order. Important order."

Petition Again After the Printing Industry Workers' Union received the instructions from the Social Affairs Bureau the night before last, it immediately notified all workers that night to resume work as usual from yesterday, but still implemented eight-hour work days. As a result, all workers went to work one after another. However, all employers insisted on nine-hour work days, otherwise they would all be refused and driven out, and the workers' meals and accommodation were stopped. Upon hearing this, the union sent Qu Shou Kang and Wang Xingquan to the Social Affairs Bureau and the Municipal Party Department to petition. Zhang Shuye and Huang Zaoxiong received them and gave a detailed account of the employers' refusal to work and eviction, requesting immediate mediation. The Printing Industry Association sent Zhang Yixin, Zhu Kehou, Wang Wenxian, and Chen Bingxi to the Social Affairs Bureau again at 3:00 PM yesterday to petition, reporting that the union had illegally notified them to continue working eight hours and requesting a strict order to stop this and stating the difficulties of not being able to work eight hours.

Official Investigation The Garrison Headquarters, the Political Department of the Public Concession Engineering Bureau, all sent personnel yesterday to investigate the truth. The Printing Industry Workers' Union sent a letter to the Engineering Bureau yesterday, saying: "Inquiry: The printing industry unrest this time was caused by the illegal shutdown of the employers, not by the improper actions of the workers leading to a strike. The responsibility issue should belong to the employers. After the employers stopped operations, they evicted workers, sealed the factory doors, etc. In order to protect local security, our association led all workers to take orderly actions and wait for the party and government agencies to resolve the issue. We are sincerely afraid that your department will misunderstand. We will first send a letter to explain in detail, and we hope that your department will not obstruct it and provide appropriate maintenance within the possible scope. We are very grateful."

Questioning Today The Social Affairs Bureau notified the Printing Industry Workers' Union and the Printing Industry Association yesterday: "Notice: According to the union's presentation, for the request to mediate the treatment conditions, this bureau has scheduled to convene a questioning session at 1:00 PM on August 5. We hereby notify you to appoint two responsible representatives to come to the bureau to wait for questioning. Special notice."

Summary of Conditions The Printing Industry Workers' Union proposed a total of 25 amendments to the treatment conditions, which were approved by the Municipal Party Department. The summary is as follows: Article 3: Eight hours of work per day. If there is night work, four hours shall be considered one work day, and two hours and a quarter shall be considered half a work day. Meal money shall be provided as usual. Double wages shall be paid for rest days, holidays, and vacation work. However, night work shall not exceed four times per week. Article 7: Employers shall subsidize workers with 8 yuan per month for navel fees and 4 yuan for accommodation fees. Workers and apprentices shall be treated equally. Article 8: Workers who do not stop working for half a month shall be promoted for two days. Those who are promoted for twelve consecutive times shall be given half a month's compensation for work. More shall be given by analogy to encourage them. Article 10: Employers shall subsidize the union's operating expenses. The methods are listed below: Factories with 10 people shall subsidize 6 yuan per month. Those with less than 10 people shall also be the same. Those with 20 people shall subsidize 2 yuan per month. Those with less than 20 people shall also be the same. Those with 30 people shall subsidize 3 yuan per month. More shall be given by analogy. Article 11: Employers shall subsidize the union's education expenses. The methods are listed below: Factories with 10 people shall subsidize 1 yuan per month for the union's education expenses. Those with less than 10 people shall also be the same. Those with 20 people shall subsidize 2 yuan per month. Those with less than 20 people shall also be the same. Those with 30 people shall subsidize 3 yuan per month. More shall be given by analogy. Article 15: Workers who continue to work for a certain period of time shall have special vacations. The methods shall be handled in accordance with the Factory Law. Article 20: After this contract is signed, employers shall increase wages according to the following methods: Those with wages within 10 yuan shall increase by 5 yuan, those with wages within 20 yuan shall increase by 4 yuan, and those with wages above 20 yuan shall increase by 3 yuan. The method of increasing wages every year thereafter shall be based on the increase in the cost of living donations and shall be publicly announced when the annual business accounts are settled. 40% of the surplus shall be used as bonuses and distributed to all workers. Article 24: Abolish all subcontracting and short-term work systems.

Li Bohan's Discussion of Foreign Merchant Title Deeds 139

A reporter from the Guowen News Agency visited Mr. Li Bohan, a member of the Standing Committee of the Shanghai Real Estate Association, regarding the issue of the Engineering Bureau Real Estate Board and title deeds. According to him, the land valuation in the Public Concession has always been presided over by Westerners, which is quite unfair. This association advocated that Chinese people should be hired for the Real Estate Board, and the Engineering Bureau has already accepted this, as seen in the bureau's gazette. However, the procedures for submission are currently being studied to comply with Article 28 of the Yangjingbang Regulations. In the future, land valuation in the concession will be held once a year, which is closely related to Chinese owners. The reporter then asked about the foreign merchant title deeds. He replied that the Shanghai foreign merchant title deeds originated from the Yangjingbang Land Regulations established in 1845. Foreign merchants who want to lease land must negotiate a price with the Chinese owners who hold the title deed and enter into a perpetual lease with a description of the terrain and address. The consulate will forward it to the Shanghai Daotai for verification and seal it, and then return it to the holder, which is called a title deed. Later, Chinese people who wanted to acquire real estate also entrusted foreign merchants to come forward, obtain the title deed, and then have the foreign merchant issue a letter of trust, noting that a certain Chinese person entrusted him to register, which is called a power deed. This kind of deformed title deed is rare in all countries and has been going on for decades. Recently, it has become even more serious, so that there are only about 5,000 acres of title deed land in the concession that have not been transferred to title deeds, and most of the title deed holders are Chinese. Chinese people pay a large amount of donations and increase the tax amount of foreign merchants, with responsibility but no rights, which is regrettable. As for its disadvantages, in small terms, untrustworthy foreign merchants often steal and sell the property that Chinese people entrust them to register, and there is no way to prosecute them, which is not uncommon. In large terms, if any foreign merchant country and China encounter similar events such as severance of diplomatic relations, the foreign merchant title deeds of that country will be confiscated or returned, and the land rights of Chinese people who entrust registration are likely to be lost. Usually, Chinese owners regard title deeds as the most reliable, and there may be a day when they are helpless. Fortunately, Mr. Wu Jingxiong, an advisor to the Engineering Bureau, has recently paid attention to the issue of foreign merchant title deeds and has a proposal to study solutions, which is a very important plan. The reporter also asked about improvement methods. He replied that the deformed title deeds held by Chinese people are caused by the unequal treaties signed under duress at that time, and there is no room for existence in principle. However, the current progress can only refer to suitable methods and ask the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to negotiate amendments to Articles 35 of the Yangjingbang Regulations.

Pedestrian Shot to Death by Random Gunfire 143

The Deceased Was Yang Lao Si

Had a Fight with Someone Last Month

There May Be Other Circumstances

Reported by the Teahouse Owner

At about 8:00 PM last night, a man was shot to death by random gunfire near the telephone pole at No. 44 South, Hongnanshan Road, Republican New Road, Zhabei. The details are as follows:

Body Examination At 8:30 PM last night, the Zhongxing Road Police Station of the Fourth District Public Security Bureau received a report from Xiao Jingqi, the owner of the Daxing Teahouse at No. 209 Hongnanshan Road, stating that someone had shot a pedestrian on Republican New Road. Patrol Captains Luo Mingqi, Cheng Jun, and Chen Ruichun immediately led police officer Cao Lizhen to investigate. They saw the deceased lying on the side of the road wearing a white shirt and shorts, a straw hat on his head, blue embroidered slippers on his feet, a leather belt around his waist, a bundle of pickled vegetables, a black fan, and a bag of nails, all scattered on the ground. There was blood everywhere. There were multiple gunshot wounds on his left leg, knee, back, and forehead. Because it was at night, it was not very clear, but there were about ten gunshot wounds in total.

Family Report While they were investigating, the deceased's family arrived after hearing the news and cried over the body. The deceased's wife, Yao, reported that the deceased's surname was Yang, named Lao Si, 40 years old, from Yancheng, and currently unemployed. He lived at No. 3, Huikang Lane, South Railway. There were two wives in the family, and no brothers or sisters, and no parents or children. Yao, 37 years old this year, and her sister (referring to the deceased's concubine) work in silk factories to make a living. He went out at 4:00 PM today to see his friend Xiao Jingqi at Hongnanshan Road, and he was shot to death for some reason. According to the deceased's concubine, her mother's surname is Lu, 21 years old, and she became acquainted with the deceased in June of this year. When she was 19 years old, she cohabited with Mao Fengxiang, who now lives in a thatched shed next to the Daping Glass Factory on Yongxing Road, behind the Sun Temple. The deceased had a fight with Ye Zigao, who now lives in a thatched shed near Xiaohong Temple on Republican New Road, last month. There may be other circumstances.

Post-Incident Investigation After obtaining the statements, the police chief and others went to the Daxing Teahouse on Hongnanshan Road to investigate. According to the owner of the teahouse, Xiao Jingqi, the deceased arrived at his store at 4:30 PM and went to the Xinyixing barber shop next door at about 5:00 PM. At about 8:00 PM, I suddenly heard gunshots. I went out to watch and learned that Yang Lao Si had been shot to death. I immediately ran to report to your police station and went to the deceased's home in Huikang Lane. The deceased and I are friends. He came to my place today to collect usury. I don't know anything else. Later, Police Chief Luo took the deceased's wife Yao, concubine Lu, and reporter Xiao Jingqi to the station and sent them to the Fourth District for interrogation. The body was guarded by Jin Ertu, the local bailiff Wang Shaoting. Today, he will be ordered to report to the Shanghai Local Court for an autopsy and try to arrest the murderer. At 11:10 PM, Ye Zigao was arrested. He claimed to be a 37-year-old from Zhenjiang and was immediately sent to the district for interrogation.

Forensic Examination Institute to be Completed Soon 150

The Ministry of Justice decided to establish a forensic examination institute in this city to handle examination matters and specially appointed Sun Kui Fang as the director of preparations. After receiving the commission, Sun came to Shanghai last summer when the First Special District Local Court was established and attached the preparatory office to the court to begin preparations. The court's examination cases were also handled by Director Sun along with the forensic doctors. Later, the Ministry of Justice, considering the urgent need for the establishment of the examination institute, allocated a large sum of money, ordering Sun to purchase several mu of land in Yangjia Bridge, Zhenru Town, and hire workers to build the institute through bidding. After half a year, the construction is nearing completion. The content is roughly divided into two parts: (1) Hospital, (2) Examination. The autopsy office of the Public Concession will also be attached to the forensic examination institute. Originally, autopsy matters in the Public Concession were handled at the autopsy office on Faelun Road. However, as the office was built by the Public Works Department of the Municipal Council, the court had to pay a certain amount for each corpse examination. If Western doctors were required to perform surgery and autopsies, the cost would be even higher. Although this money was used to cover the expenses of the office and its hospital, the annual expenditure for the court was surprisingly high. Now that the examination is moved to Zhenru, this expense can be avoided. Director Sun is currently stationed at the site, directing all arrangements, as the construction of the institute is nearing completion and the internal layout still needs to be arranged. In addition to the existing forensic talents, it is said that more will be hired and are currently being sought. Although the official opening date has not been determined, it should be in the near future. Autopsy matters in the First Special District will be moved there after the official opening of the institute. From now on, the important policy of examination can be said to follow in the footsteps of justice, break away from foreign influence, and become transcendent and independent.

Wusong Water Police

Rectification and Issuance of Fishing Boat Flag Licenses 152

Zhang Han, the former director of the Fourth District of the Wusong Water Police, believed that imported fishing boats were inevitably mixed with good and bad elements. Therefore, he drafted measures for issuing flag licenses to eliminate bandit traces. The proposal was approved by the 379th meeting of the Jiangsu Provincial Government Committee. The Fourth District Department then hired boats and sent personnel to conduct inspections. However, the flag license fees collected exceeded the prescribed amount by more than ten times, and even extra demands were made, which caused great suffering to the boat owners. Since Jiang Chaoxiong took over as the director of the Fourth District, he realized that the previous method of hiring boats and sending personnel was not perfect and was prone to abuse. However, as the case was related to eliminating bandits and had been approved by the provincial government, it should be continued to maintain the authority of the law. In order to fundamentally eliminate abuses, he ordered the 16th team of the district to continue handling the matter temporarily, conduct serious inspections, and issue fishing boat flag licenses according to regulations. According to the regulations, each flag license only charges a material fee of four jiao, and no extra demands are allowed. If there is any obstruction, once discovered or accused, it will be strictly investigated. Team Leader Zhang Zongliang has begun to implement the inspection since yesterday after receiving the order.

Various Organizations

Supporting the Hua Chang Paint False Accusation Case 154

Confiscated Paint Can Be Returned Soon, Detained Personnel to Be Released

Feixing Brand Sanitary Paint produced by Hua Chang Oil Mill is made from useless scraps of leather and chemical solutions. It is used to paint utensils, making them bright, durable, and odorless. It has long been approved by the Central Sanitary Testing Institute as non-toxic and issued a certificate. The National Trademark Registration Bureau of the former Ministry of Industry and Commerce approved Feixing as a trademark. Since its introduction, it has been favored by various sectors of the country. Unexpectedly, the Hangzhou branch of the factory was falsely accused by someone in the Zhejiang Provincial Civil Affairs Department of using sanitary paint as a substitute for opium. On July 17, the Civil Affairs Department confiscated hundreds of cans of paint and detained two employees. The next day, they sent personnel to Shanghai, along with Chinese and Western detectives from the Shanghai Municipal Police and Yangshupu Police Station, to investigate the factory on Huasheng Road. As a result, no contraband was found. After the incident occurred, the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, the Chinese National Goods Maintenance Association, and the Joint Association of Machine-Made National Goods Factories, after inquiring, believed that the sanitary paint produced by the Hua Chang Factory had long been approved by the government and was non-toxic. They sent telegrams to the Zhejiang Provincial Government and the Civil Affairs Department to investigate thoroughly in order to protect national goods. Yesterday, the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce also telegraphed the Provincial Government and the Civil Affairs Department. The telegram said, (omitted above) "The Hua Chang Factory has been in operation for many years, and its products have been tested and certified by the Central Chemistry Institute, so they must be non-toxic. According to the factory's letter, (omitted in the middle) it seems to be true. We hereby request your government and department to investigate and return the original items, and punish the false accuser to clarify the truth and alleviate the difficulties of merchants. We hope so." It is also reported that the Zhejiang Civil Affairs Department, after receiving telegrams from various groups in this city proving the case, will return the confiscated paint and release the detained personnel soon.

New Stage

Manager and Shareholders Extorted 160

Caused by Anger from Dismissed Teahouse Employee

Wang Yongshan, the manager of the New Stage in Mongol Road, Zhabei, received two extortion letters on the 24th and 25th of last month, demanding 100 yuan. The letters instructed Wang to leave the money in a paper basket under the telephone pole at the tram stop of the 18th Road at the Garbage Bridge on the 27th. After receiving the letters, Wang immediately reported the case to the First Police Station of the Fourth District Public Security Bureau. The police chief ordered plainclothes officers to go to the designated location to wait, but there was no movement. On the 29th, Wang Yongshan received another letter, signed "Unemployed," with similar wording to the previous letters. The police station sent people again, but still to no avail. On the 2nd of this month, Tang Ziliang, a shareholder of the New Stage, received another extortion letter with a postmark from Daji Road, Ximen, demanding 1,000 yuan. The letter instructed him to wrap the money in red paper and send it to the back of the water pillar at the entrance of the Continental Bank No. 2 Warehouse at the New Garbage Bridge at 1:00 AM on the 3rd. After receiving the news, the First Police Station of the Fourth District Public Security Bureau ordered the manager of the New Stage to submit all the account books and compare the handwriting in the letter. It was found that the handwriting was similar to that of Hu Chengtang, the teahouse employee who had been dismissed from the stage. It was also learned that Hu often went to the Pinfang Teahouse on Mongol Road to drink tea. Therefore, the police went to the address at 6:00 PM on the afternoon of the 3rd and arrested Hu. Under interrogation, Hu confessed that he was caused by the oppression of Wang and Tang. After being dismissed last month, the deposit of 30 yuan had not been returned. Out of anger, he resorted to this strategy. He also claimed that he did not go to collect the money after sending the letters and did not know that he had violated the law.

Hu Baogen Denies Being Sheng Baida 161

Waiting for Wujin County to Provide Evidence for Further Verification

Hu Baogen, also known as Sheng Baida, from Changzhou, fled to Shanghai the other day to evade a kidnapping case in his hometown and hid in the Kunming Hotel at No. 35 Kunming Road. Xue Renquan, a detective from the local Public Security Bureau, learned of this and followed him to Shanghai. He reported the case to the Huishan Police Station and requested assistance in the arrest. The police chief sent Chinese Detective Cao Xirong No. 665 and a secret Chinese officer to arrest Hu and take him to the police station for detention. Yesterday morning, he was sent to the Third Court of the Special Court. According to Zhang Tianyin, the lawyer of the police station, the defendant denied that his other name was Sheng Baida and that the name on the arrest warrant did not match. The police station requested the Wujin County Government to provide conclusive evidence that the defendant had committed kidnapping and extortion in Changzhou. There was no objection to the transfer of the case. Subsequently, Detective Xue Renquan testified that the defendant was known as Sheng Baida in the Beimen area of Changzhou, and many accomplices had also been arrested. He then presented the official letter for inspection. The defendant claimed that his real name was Hu Baogen and that he did not have the alias Sheng Baida. He denied committing a kidnapping case in his hometown. Judge Shen Bingrong verified the confession and ordered the case to be postponed to the morning of the 11th of this month for the Wujin County Government to provide evidence for further verification. The defendant was returned to custody.

Inspection of the Murder of Wife in West Shanghai 162

Shen A'gen, a farmer residing at No. 5, Jinjia Lane, North End, Caohejing Town, West Shanghai, killed his wife He a few days ago. This has been reported in various newspapers. It is now learned that the murderer Shen A'gen is 31 years old. His first wife, Hu, died of illness in August last year. In the winter, Shen A'gen spent 200 yuan on a tea gift to marry He, a woman from Chongming, as his second wife. The couple was still in harmony. However, Shen A'gen suddenly suffered from mental illness in March this spring. He spoke incoherently, was capricious, and talked to himself all day long. There were no unusual signs before the incident. In addition to A'gen and his wife, there were only his widowed sister-in-law Wang and two young nieces in the house, but they had already separated. Wang and her two daughters lived in the east end of the hall, while the deceased lived in the west end. There were no neighbors. Wang made a living by selling vegetables. Every morning at 3:00 AM, she carried a basket to the market. Therefore, A'gen must have killed He around 5:00 AM. Later, A'gen ran around in front of the house, looking like a madman. At that time, it was already dawn. The villagers went to the fields to hoe weeds. When asked why he was wandering here, he said he was selling dead people's heads, 300 yuan each. Then a member of the clan entered the house, calling for his wife He. He walked to the door and saw that He had been killed on the ground in a pool of blood. He then reported to the Sixth District Third Branch. Officer Yuan and Chief Wang led the police to the scene. When the murderer saw the police coming to arrest him, he jumped into the river and fled. He was caught by the police officer Fu Congdian in the river after six or seven rivers. He was taken back to the station. After Chief Liu's preliminary trial, Shen A'gen spoke vaguely and did not answer the questions. It was observed that there were many wounds on his body. Yesterday, a written statement was prepared and sent to the bureau for interrogation. At about 4:00 PM in the afternoon, Prosecutor Wu Deying appointed by the court brought the examiner to the scene for examination. It was found that the deceased's neck was cut with a knife, the trachea was severed, and the head was about to fall off. There were also many knife wounds on the arms and chest. It was determined that she had been stabbed to death. The coroner ordered the family to collect the body and await further investigation.

Anti-Opium Association Issues Declaration Yesterday 163

Seventh Anniversary Today

Today is the seventh anniversary of the Chinese National Anti-Opium Association. Since its establishment, the association has made remarkable achievements. Considering that there is still much work to be done in the future, and the progress of the cause depends on the support of the people of the country, a declaration is issued to state the feelings of the past year and the hopes for the future. The declaration of the association is as follows: "On August 5th of the 13th year of the Republic of China, this association was entrusted with the will of 400 million compatriots and maintained by the strength of more than 40 organizations. It was born in response to the times and bears the mission of developing Dr. Sun Yat-sen's anti-opium instructions and eliminating the scourge of opium in order to clear the black terror. For seven years, this aspiration has not been slackened. We have used the analogy of floods and fierce beasts to awaken the people of the country, and with tears of sorrow, we have used firmness to unite the people's will. The promotion of the anti-opium movement has been far-reaching. Internally, we have cultivated the public opinion against opium, and externally, we have aroused the sympathy of friendly countries, so that the rampant spread of opium has not reached a state of inhumanity, and opium merchants have not dared to be without fear. This small achievement, this association dares not exaggerate, nor dare to hide. It is necessary to provide the public with real facts for national judgment. However, as the sky asks for misfortune and human desires flow, opium, which is recognized by the world as a tool for destroying the country and exterminating the race, is regarded as a source of profit, like flies chasing stench and ants clinging to rancidness. As a result, our people engaged in anti-opium often sigh that the more they try to control the situation, the more chaotic it becomes. The so-called 'The Tao is one foot high, the devil is ten feet high,' we deeply feel this pain. In this harsh environment, although this association has been full of thorns and difficult to walk, we have sometimes hesitated and thought of giving up. But at the thought of the association bearing a great responsibility and the people's earnest expectations, we cannot help but immediately become excited and angry, and engage in a bloody battle with the evil forces again. The association and anti-opium comrades in various places are devising ways to defeat the enemy, while the enemy is also rising up to engage in a large-scale union. Celebrities, officials, local vendors, opium merchants, and even local bullies and hooligans, all gather under the same opium protection banner to fight against the people who sincerely adhere to Dr. Sun Yat-sen's instructions. Their power is strong, their conspiracies are endless, and they often use imperialism as their backing and government officials as their confidants. If we uncover the inside story of the major opium cases in the past, there is hardly a case that does not involve these characters, or even the main actors who perform on stage. In the case of the Shanghai Jianghai Customs seizing a large batch of opium from the Kloseau, Japanese people are engaged in this business, German ships are financing its transportation, and government offices are protecting it. Therefore, many incidents have occurred, but there has been no official disposal of the opium, and there is even news of a full refund. In the case of the false accusation against Mr. and Mrs. Huang Jiahuai, the secretary-general of this association, celebrities who advocated public sales of opium, local vendors who poisoned the country, colluded to trap them, and senior officials also sat in conspiracy to implement the opium public sales policy. Those who advocated this were medical doctors and opium suppression officials. Those who expressed their agreement were government tax collection agencies and local tyrants who relied on opium for a living. This association, considering this move as a dead end for the country and a black luck for China's doomsday, ran around calling for help, vowed to oppose it, and the opium suppression authorities deceived and acted deceptively. They immediately concealed the name of opium public sales and changed it to the Opium Suppression and Investigation Office to forcibly implement it. Since its establishment, strange phenomena have emerged, and foxes and dogs have occupied important positions. The ruffians and local merchants have become officials. This is an unprecedented and bizarre phenomenon. This association, lamenting the worsening situation and the increasingly fierce trend, believes that a bloody battle to the death is imminent. Without any regard for ourselves, we raise our arms and shout, rushing and pouncing. Fortunately, the people's hearts have not died, and public opinion is still strong. The people are united and respond as one, competing to make serious representations to the government, stripping the villainous souls of rebellion, and the opium suppression authorities are also afraid of the people's feelings and the need to ease the atmosphere. They resolutely abandoned this policy, and then there was a clear order to abolish the Opium Suppression and Investigation Office. Recently, according to rumors from various sources, the advocates of public sales, because their ambitions have failed, have not been able to achieve their long-cherished wish to be promoted and make a fortune. Because their evil intentions have not died, they have repeatedly proposed new schemes and have re-recommended the establishment of a Narcotic Drug Administration. The name is more clever, the evils are more numerous. In the past, it was only limited to the public sale of opium, but now it will also include morphine, heroin, and all narcotics for public sale. The so-called medical doctor is insane and has gone so far. Alas, Heavens, who is he? With the desire for profit from one or two people, he wants to sacrifice the future of the party and the country and the lives of 400 million compatriots. Isn't this a heinous crime? This association has always adhered to the policy of eliminating evil and is determined to suppress opium, maintain the spirit of rejecting opium, and develop Dr. Sun Yat-sen's instructions. It vows to fight this group of people who fatten themselves by selling opium. From now on, no matter what kind of opium suppression measures with public sales characteristics violate Dr. Sun Yat-sen's instructions, this association also vows to resist with all its strength. It must be known that the disaster of destroying the country and exterminating the race is imminent, and there is no room for us to stand by and watch. If people do not harm beasts, beasts will also harm people. It is better to be a broken jade than a whole tile. We hope that next year today, this association can comfort the people of the country with the most satisfying text, with the quickness of the scourge of opium being eliminated or sharply reduced. This depends on the future efforts of this association and the actual support of the people. This declaration is made."

Ministries of Industry and Interior Draft 17 Fishery Regulations

Circulars Sent to Provincial and Municipal Governments for Active Preparation

Riri News says that the Ministry of Industry believes that the fishery industry in China has been declining in recent years for three reasons: First, it is invaded by foreign ships; second, it lacks technology; and third, local government offices have no protection. Municipal Chamber of Commerce Responds

Lending Interest Practices of Silver and Money Businesses 167

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce yesterday responded to Certified Public Accountant Jiang Xin Zhao, stating that it had previously received a letter regarding the handling of interest disputes on loans, and listed two points for inquiry regarding the regulations and customs of the silver and money industries, requesting a reply for reference. After forwarding letters to the Silver and Money Businesses Association of the city, the Money Businesses Association replied on July 31, stating, "(1) The interest rate for regular loans in the money industry, unless there is a contract stipulating otherwise, is determined at the discretion of the market based on the urgency of supply and demand. Article 7, Paragraph 1 of the Shanghai Money Industry Business Regulations stipulates that the maximum interest rate for inter-bank lending among the same industry is 7 mace per thousand taels. Article 7, Paragraph 4 stipulates that the outstanding interest is based on the interest on current deposits, with each member adding discretionarily. If the interest on current deposits is less than 4 taels and 5 mace, it is still based on 4 taels and 5 mace. Although there is no fixed standard for the so-called discretionary addition to the current deposit interest, there must be a verbal agreement between the bank and the customer. (2) The settlement period for regular loan interest in the money industry, unless there is a contract stipulating otherwise, is once at the end of each month. The interest settled in the previous month is added to the principal of the current month for compound interest calculation." On the 3rd of this month, the reply from the Bankers Association stated that the bank's regular loans are mostly contracted. There are also methods that imitate money shops, discretionarily adding 4 taels or 4 taels and 5 mace, which depends on the market, although there is no fixed standard, banks and customers must have a verbal agreement. The settlement period for interest, unless otherwise stipulated in the contract, is generally every six months or twelve months. If the principal and interest are not cleared, the interest is included in the principal for compound interest calculation. According to this, the respective replies are recorded and provided for review and filing.

Local Autonomy

Second Enrollment for the Training Institute 169

Registration Begins Tomorrow

Examination on the 16th and 17th

The Municipal Government, in order to actively prepare for local autonomy, established a local autonomy training institute in December of last year to cultivate service personnel. The first class of students has completed their studies and internships, and graduation certificates have been issued. The screening and distribution for probation have been reported previously. Now it is known that since the Municipal Government revised the charter of the institute, the mayor concurrently serves as the director, and Ji Zongxing has been appointed as the deputy director. The various sections of the second enrollment and commencement are now being actively carried out. Yesterday, the first preparatory meeting of the second enrollment was held and it was resolved to start reporting from tomorrow, and the entrance examination will be held on the 16th and 17th of this month. Any junior high school graduates or those who have worked in administrative affairs for more than one year in organizations affiliated to the National Government and have been recommended by the Party Department and municipal agencies may take the examination. The examination is divided into three tests: the first test is a physical examination, the second test is a written test, and the third test is an oral test. The written test is divided into subjects such as Chinese, Party ideology, arithmetic, science, history, and geography. The duration of the study period is set at two years. In addition to paying half of the fees for food and uniforms, the rest is free. The quota is set at 100 students. The Municipal Government has increased the funding for the institute and will build a school building in the city center.

Admonishing Against Sleeping in the Streets 174

The French Concession Police recently said that because the weather is hot, the residents in the concession sleep outdoors on both sides of the road every night. This is seen everywhere on the main streets and alleys, which is very harmful to hygiene. Therefore, special instructions have been given to the Chinese and Western detectives and patrolmen to advise people to go home to sleep at any time when they are on duty in order to emphasize hygiene.

Watermelon Prices Soar 175

Since the continuous plum rain in this city, the weather has been cool, and watermelons are on the market, but few people patronize them, resulting in a sharp drop in prices. Each load is sold for only two yuan, and because there is too much rain, the watermelons are not sweet. Therefore, watermelon vendors are suffering. In recent days, the weather has suddenly changed, and it has become extremely hot. Watermelon vendors are having great luck. Yesterday, the price of watermelons on the market was actually seven yuan per load, and there were very few goods arriving. The watermelon vendors made three times the profit and returned with smiles on their faces.
